<rate>1</rate><Text>Strongly disappointed.

As I have read articles about this place and the chef, me and my wife decided to give a shot for this Valentine's day.

The results were a nightmare.

We made a reservation and arrived on time, but the host told us that we should wait about 15 minutes. I expected any kind of apologies for this, but there were none. No comments at all.

Once we were seated, we found outdoor tables and utensils were not clean. This started to decrease the appetite and Valentine's day vibe.

Regarding the foods, we ordered aguachile and jamaica taco. Aguachile was tasty yet its plating was slightly unorganized. I started to think maybe the chef was off duty...? Anyway, aguachile was overall good.
However, jamaica taco was way too dry and mushrooms were too chewy. I guess cooking mushrooms softer and adding more sauces in it might help.

I am not a professional critic, so maybe I am not the right person to judge the foods quality, but I do not like them compared to other mexican dinings with a similar price level.

Overall, I would not recommend this place and do not think I will revisit.

We thought maybe it was busy and she was just inexperienced, but it wasn't busy so there's no possible excuse for the pathetic treatment. We stopped here while we were driving through the area.   I've had Avatar's Punjabi burrito before and thought it was ok, but not as good as Curry Up Now.   I found the enchiladas we ordered at this location quite excellent and look forward to coming back.

We had the smoked eggplant and mixed vegetables, both of which were good and had different sauces and thus pretty different tastes (and it isn't weird to order both for the same table). They are smothered in sauce so it isn't the easiest to eat as takeout.

We also ordered the mushrooms appetizer and some fries (for the kid) and neither of these dishes were things I would want to order again.  The fries were too soft and the mushrooms far too oily.<//text>

An absolute Bay Area favorite! The owner is definitely one of the highlights of this restaurant. If you are a new customer and are unsure on what to order the owner is more than willing to surprise you with some dishes according to your taste preference. This place is the perfect balance of Indian and fusion flavors. Make sure not to miss the enchiladas! The last time I visited I had the  spinach fettuccini that was amazingly delicious. The pasta made in house with spinach, millet flour and mustard greens, so creative and tasty!<//Review>

<Text>The best thing about this place is the owner - chef. He maintains it a point to go and talk to each customer and offer his recommendations.
He made the conversation so interesting, throwing in quizzes to guess the ingredients in lieu of free food, which of course we couldn't win.
In the end he also gave us some free vegetables from his kitchen garden which are not easy to find in US.
Amazing Vegetarian Food, You don't even need to look at the menu, he will take it upon himself to make something new exclusively for u..

This is the art of marketing by winning hearts!<//Text>< Pics>

< review>
My aunt recommended me to try Avatar's. I really loved the fusion food served at Avatar's - full of taste, care, smile and happiness. The reason I say all of this is because not just the food but our entire experience at this restaurant was amazing.

Ashok, the owner cum chef of the restaurant was very welcoming, walked us through his specialities and why he used certain ingredients and why he did not. He offered us the freedom to be able to customize the dishes to our taste and health choices - like protein, carbs etc.

We ordered Jerky Chicken dish which was more inclined towards Jamaican cuisine. We also order ground lamb enchiladas which was a combination of Indian and Mexican flavor. Both the dishes were very tasty and we relished every bit of it.

The restaurant has decent sized free parking lot available in front of it.

Prices are appropriate for the taste that you get here. The owner cum chef has definitely put in a lot of effort to customize the dishes and create an amazing blend of Jamaican, Mexican and Indian flavors.

I would definitely recommend you to try out Avatar's! In Ashok's words, it might be one of the best food you ever had!

Thank you for your support!</review>

< review>
Nice Indian restaurant with a twist. We went after it was mentioned in the Check please (KQED) program. The offer a couple traditional Indian appetizers, like Samosa. The entrees have both a Mexican twist, i.e., chicken enchiladas but the spicing is all Indian. The Italian style entrees are Indian entrees served on a bed of zucchini spaghetti, etc. But the kicker is actually different, the chef/owner of the place asks if he can bring entrees of his choice. Three vegetarians on the table went with that option - they were quite happy with the selection. I went with the chicken enchiladas, very good interesting flavors - Indian, plus traditional Mexican flavors and the side rice is Indian style. The owner makes a fun game out of the chef's choice entrees - he asks you to guess what the vegetables are, if you get all of them right the entire meal is free! I don't know if anyone got all right, we gave up about 30% of the way.

The place is a bit small, so cozy is the word. It can get crowded. Note in Google maps directions - it asks you to take that last right and claims.you've arrived... Not really you have to turn into the strip and the 3rd place is Avatar's.

Bottom line, worth a visit.<//review>

<user_name>Biren Parmar</user_name>< Pictures>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< UserId.>
112306781013376612499< /UserId.>
<review>This review focuses on the vegetarian dishes we had at Avatar's. Imagine being able to order flavorful dishes made from ingredients used in traditional Indian cooking, an alien concept in a vast majority of Indian restaurants in the US. I personally don't have a problem with the Indian restaurant experience, but after a while, it starts to get repetitive - it's the same set of dishes on the menu everywhere (at least this seems to be the case for the vegetarian section of the menu). The guys at Avatar's excel at using not-so-commonly used veggies and greens in their preparations. Then, they take it up a notch and make fusion dishes out of these ingredients, which is simply mind blowing. The entire experience of the visit was awesome, not very different from some of the other reviewers here. Definitely going back.
An afterthought: We had been a little skeptical about going to the place after an underwhelming experience at one of the other branches of Avatar's in the area months ago. But the amount of positive feedback we got about the place, especially even from non-Indians, made the itch to pay a visit at least once irresistible. This is a completely different and unique experience.< /review></record>

We will return to San Francisco, and to Avatar's, without a doubt.<//review>

< review>
This is by far the best Indian restaurant in the Bay Area. I make this bold statement as an Indian person with a talented cook for a mother and countless experiences eating at Indian restaurants while growing up in the area. This restaurant best exemplifies healthy, tasteful Indian cuisine, as well as some incredible fusion dishes (I had to go back several times to try all the Punjabi enchiladas). The masala chai is always freshly made to order, and you can be confident that anything you order is made with the best ingredients.

By food quality alone this place deserves 5 stars. The owner, a delightful man who greets every customer and takes every order, will make your experience personalized and extraordinary. Aside from his deep knowledge as a nutritionist, he is deeply engaged in the customer experience and is a perfect example of how to run a successful business for decades. Just as his food exemplifies healthy and tasteful food of India, his personality exemplifies the work ethic and dharmic sense of responsibility of India.

This is truly one of the hidden gems of California and I whole-heartedly recommend this restaurant to everyone.<//review>
